          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3241018299" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1863444699687444032">Trigger warnings: racism, racial slurs, violence, racially motivated violence, implied lynchings.<br/><br/>I first read this book back in the late 90s when I studied it for English in year 8 or 9, and I remember really enjoying it. So when I saw it on the shelf at the library, I figured it was time for a reread. I initially struggled to get into this one, but ultimately I thoroughly enjoyed it. <br/><br/>It's similar in a lot of ways to the stalwart of high school English, To Kill a Mockingbird, and I will be etern</span>
  <span id="freeText1863444699687444032" style="display:none">Trigger warnings: racism, racial slurs, violence, racially motivated violence, implied lynchings.<br /><br />I first read this book back in the late 90s when I studied it for English in year 8 or 9, and I remember really enjoying it. So when I saw it on the shelf at the library, I figured it was time for a reread. I initially struggled to get into this one, but ultimately I thoroughly enjoyed it. <br /><br />It's similar in a lot of ways to the stalwart of high school English, To Kill a Mockingbird, and I will be eternally grateful that my high school chose to assign us a book by an African-American author from an African-American perspective and dealing with the serious racist bullshit that people had to live with rather than TKAM, a story that deals with racism from the perspective of a white kid by a white author and that ends VERY badly for the African-American character. <br /><br />I think this one stands on its own pretty well despite being part of a series, and I'm really glad I decided to reread it. </span>
  <a data-text-id="1863444699687444032" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('qDH22CbhJszdpZHq4aoDZRaERSG0oiZ/kISqCeoqn6mSF58Knb/vpHqOJYsWXwm6wNui6XovqBjL+uy4J2ltMw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('GQgh7O3+zqur9yFsQt9zzrQthVG2mcPzmwOPO7Y4zwcjLkg+VqAHwwzclQ21KnkRYnJimXgUTZTAfcmKe3s9nQ==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/26946.Mildred_D_Taylor">About Mildred D. Taylor</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer12714642547614129116">Mildred DeLois Taylor is an African-American writer known for her works exploring the struggle faced by African-American families in the Deep South.<br/><br/>Taylor was born in Jackson, Mississippi, but lived there only a short amount of time, then moved to Toledo, Ohio, where she spent most of her childhood. She now lives in Colorado with her daughter. <br/><br/>Many of her works are based on stories of her family t</span>
  <span id="freeText12714642547614129116" style="display:none">Mildred DeLois Taylor is an African-American writer known for her works exploring the struggle faced by African-American families in the Deep South.<br /><br />Taylor was born in Jackson, Mississippi, but lived there only a short amount of time, then moved to Toledo, Ohio, where she spent most of her childhood. She now lives in Colorado with her daughter. <br /><br />Many of her works are based on stories of her family that she heard while growing up. She has stated that these anecdotes became very clear in her mind, and in fact, once she realized that adults talked about the past, "I began to visualize all the family who had once known the land, and I felt as if I knew them, too ..." Taylor has talked about how much history was in the stories; some stories took place during times of slavery and some post-slavery.<br /><br />Taylor's most famous book is <em>Roll of Thunder, Hear My Cry</em>. In 1977, the book won the Newbery Medal. <em>Roll of Thunder, Hear My Cry</em> is the middle book, chronologically, in the Logans series that also includes titles such as <em>The Land</em>, <em>Song of the Trees</em>, <em>Let the Circle Be Unbroken</em>, and <em>The Road to Memphis</em>. Her collective contributions to children's literature resulted in her being awarded the inaugural NSK Neustadt Prize for Children's Literature in 2003.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12714642547614129116" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>

Cassie Logan, first met in Song of the Trees and Roll of Thunder, Hear My Cry, is a young woman now, searching for her place in the world, a journey that takes her from Toledo to California, to law school in Boston, and, ultimately, in the 60s, home to Mississippito participate in voter registration. She is witness to the now-historic events of the century: the Great Migration north, the rise of the civil rights movement, preceded and precipitated by the racist society of America, and the often violent confrontations that brought about change. Rich, compelling storytelling is Ms. Taylor\'s hallmark, and she fulfills expectations as she brings to a close the stirring family story that has absorbed her for over forty years.
